**Proxy mismatch: ÔÇťdefect pronenessÔÇŁ is not the same as ÔÇťrefactorability.ÔÇŁ** Many results connect metrics to defects, effort, or prediction performance, which are informative but indirect proxies for ÔÇťease of automated transformation.ÔÇŁ Causal direction can be confounded (e.g., complex modules both change more and have more defects). ţłÇciteţłéturn35view3ţłéturn37view0ţłéturn19view1ţłü  

**Measurement instability across representations and projects.** Tool and representation differences (line diff vs AST diff; coarse vs fine AST) can change conclusions about edit-script size and ÔÇťcloseness to developer intent.ÔÇŁ ţłÇciteţłéturn34view0ţłéturn32view4ţłü  

**Thresholds are rarely universal.** Even where a threshold is proposed (e.g., support count ~10 as strong), authors typically acknowledge normalization and project dependence; Clio-style tools seek thresholds by maximizing accuracy per dataset. ţłÇciteţłéturn16view1ţłéturn17view1ţłü  

**Historical coupling depends on adequate history and clean transactions.** Co-change signals can be noisy (mega-commits, formatting-only commits, mixed-purpose commits), and some studies explicitly treat history sufficiency and threshold selection as open concerns. ţłÇciteţłéturn17view3ţłéturn16view6ţłü  

**AI evaluation threats: contamination and specification ambiguity.** AI/refinement studies explicitly worry that datasets might be in training data and create new datasets; they also show that vague comments and model fallacies drive failuresÔÇölimitations that are orthogonal to code metrics but interact with them (semantic cohesion can reduce ambiguity, but cannot remove it). ţłÇciteţłéturn45view4ţłéturn46view4ţłéturn21view0ţłü  

### Open problems especially relevant to AI-assisted, safe refactoring

**Metric-aware equivalence checking for general refactorings.** Translation validation is compelling as a paradigm (ÔÇťverify each transformationÔÇŁ), but extending practical equivalence checking beyond compiler transformations to refactoring rewrites across languages and frameworks remains difficult. ţłÇciteţłéturn41view4ţłéturn43view5ţłü  

**Combining semantic cohesion with dependency locality into robust ÔÇťrefactor chunks.ÔÇŁ** We have strong evidence that semantic signals align with human perception and that propagation/locality measures capture structural blast radius; building stable chunking algorithms that jointly optimize these objectivesÔÇöand that remain robust under code evolutionÔÇöis still largely a research frontier. ţłÇciteţłéturn21view0ţłéturn29view4ţłéturn30view2ţłü  

**Auditable agentic workflows.** Early evidence from iterative refactoring experiments shows convergence behavior, but we lack standardized, widely accepted audit formats that record prompt settings, metric deltas, artifact selection, and verification evidence in a way that is interoperable across tools and organizations. ţłÇciteţłéturn46view6ţłéturn45view4ţłéturn41view0ţłü  

**Regression risk prediction under refactoring vs behavior change.** Refactoring-specific bug association rates (e.g., 15% overall with strong variation by refactoring type) indicate the need for models that differentiate ÔÇťpure refactorÔÇŁ from ÔÇťtangled change,ÔÇŁ but reliable automated labeling remains challenging and sensitive to detection tooling. ţłÇciteţłéturn24view0ţłéturn32view4ţłü

10.
# Empirical Evidence on Module, File, and Token Size vs Software Quality

## Executive summary

Across decades of empirical software engineering, ÔÇťsizeÔÇŁ (module/file/method length; lines changed; sometimes token-based proxies) is consistently associated with quality outcomesÔÇöbut **the association is not a single monotone ÔÇťsmaller is always betterÔÇŁ law**. Strong studies show three recurring patterns:

First, **larger units tend to contain more *absolute* faults**, and size often remains a strong predictor even after controlling for other factors in industrial release studies. A canonical example is a file-level fault-count model on two large industrial systems where the coefficient on log(LOC) is near 1, consistent with faults roughly proportional to LOC once other factors are controlled; change status and history still matter strongly. ţłÇciteţłéturn22view0ţłü

Second, **size frequently loses explanatory power once you condition on change/process history** (how often code is touched, how big and recent changes are, etc.). In an unusually detailed industrial change-history study, change history variables dominate; once the number of changes is accounted for, LOC provides little extra predictive power for future faults. ţłÇciteţłéturn21view0ţłü

Third, many ÔÇťsize is badÔÇŁ claims are **highly sensitive to (a) the outcome definition (fault *count* vs fault *density* vs change-induced defects vs build failures), (b) the unit of analysis (file/class/module vs change/commit vs build), and (c) confounding/collinearity**. A widely cited demonstration shows that many OO metrics appeared predictive until controlling for size; afterward, their associations disappearedÔÇöan explicit caution that practitioners can mistake ÔÇťmetric correlates with sizeÔÇŁ for ÔÇťmetric independently predicts quality.ÔÇŁ ţłÇciteţłéturn25view0ţłéturn26view3ţłü

Recent large-scale MSR work strengthens the case that **ÔÇťchange sizeÔÇŁ (lines/files touched) is a practical, robust risk signal** for short-term quality outcomes (defect-inducing commits, CI build failures). In a large multi-project just-in-time quality assurance study, size-related change factors (e.g., lines added/deleted; lines of code in file before change; number of files touched) show statistically significant, context-dependent odds ratios across OSS and commercial systems. ţłÇciteţłéturn2view0ţłéturn30view0ţłéturn30view1ţłü A separate MSR study on 1,090 projects and 3.6M builds finds that higher changed-lines and changed-files measures correlate with unsuccessful builds with small-to-medium standardized effects. ţłÇciteţłéturn38view0ţłéturn39view3ţłü

Practical wording that best matches the evidence is: **ÔÇťSize is a useful risk proxy, but it is not a standalone quality goal. Prefer reviewable change sizes and keep local units small enough to understandÔÇöwhile monitoring coupling, churn, and fragmentation costs.ÔÇŁ** This phrasing aligns with both the strongest industrial observational studies and controlled maintenance/comprehension experiments. ţłÇciteţłéturn21view0ţłéturn22view0ţłéturn40view0ţłéturn44view0ţłü

## Scope, definitions, and evidence standards

This report focuses on **empirical** (measured) relationships between (a) *module/file/method size* and related size proxies and (b) quality outcomes: defects/faults, maintainability and maintenance effort, comprehension and activity cost, and change failure (e.g., build failures; defect-inducing changes). ţłÇciteţłéturn46view0ţłéturn21view0ţłéturn2view0ţłéturn44view0ţłü

### What ÔÇťsizeÔÇŁ means in the cited studies

ÔÇťSizeÔÇŁ is operationalized in multiple ways:

- **Static size of a code unit**: LOC/SLOC per file or class; method SLOC; sometimes ÔÇťlines of code in file before the change.ÔÇŁ ţłÇciteţłéturn22view0ţłéturn26view2ţłéturn30view0ţłéturn40view0ţłü  
- **Change size**: lines added/deleted/modified; number of files/directories/subsystems touched; churn ratios. ţłÇciteţłéturn30view0ţłéturn32view0ţłéturn2view0ţłéturn38view0ţłü  
- **Token-count proxies**: often captured indirectly through Halstead-style counts or similar token-based complexity measures; these are discussed as part of the broader ÔÇťsize/complexity correlatedÔÇŁ family and sometimes embedded in composite indices (e.g., maintainability index variants). ţłÇciteţłéturn40view0ţłéturn20view0ţłéturn46view0ţłü  

### Evidence-strength rubric used here

The ÔÇťstrongestÔÇŁ studies emphasized below generally have one or more of:

- **Large, longitudinal datasets** (multi-release industrial systems; many projects/builds). ţłÇciteţłéturn22view0ţłéturn21view0ţłéturn38view0ţłéturn39view3ţłü  
- **Explicit statistical modeling with controls** (e.g., negative binomial / Poisson GLMs; logistic regression with odds ratios; survival models). ţłÇciteţłéturn22view0ţłéturn21view0ţłéturn2view0ţłéturn16view0ţłü  
- **Clear threats-to-validity discussion and/or replication artifacts** (public datasets, code, or at least repeatable pipeline on public repositories). ţłÇciteţłéturn40view0ţłéturn39view3ţłéturn30view0ţłü  

## Defects and fault-proneness evidence

### File/class/module size and fault counts in large systems

A classic industrial result models **expected fault counts per file** using **negative binomial regression** to handle overdispersed count data, incorporating file code attributes and history-based predictors. The study spans **two large industrial systems** (one with **17 quarterly releases over 4 years**, another with **9 releases over 2 years**) and evaluates predictive concentration: the top 20% most fault-prone files (by prediction) contain **71%ÔÇô92%** of observed faults, averaging **83%**. ţłÇciteţłéturn22view0ţłü

Importantly for ÔÇťsizeÔÇŁ:

- The coefficient on **log(LOC)** is reported as **1.047**, with a confidence interval including 1.0ÔÇöinterpretable as being **consistent with faults proportional to LOC** once controlling for other variables, i.e., (approximately) **constant fault density** in that modelÔÇÖs sense. ţłÇciteţłéturn22view0ţłü  
- Change status has large multiplicative effects: ÔÇťchanged filesÔÇŁ and ÔÇťnew filesÔÇŁ are estimated at about **2.9├Ś** and **6.4├Ś** the expected faults, respectively, all else equal (via exponentiated coefficients). ţłÇciteţłéturn22view0ţłü  

This study is strong for external validity within ÔÇťlarge industrial release engineering,ÔÇŁ but its **unit is file**, its defect definition is aligned to that environment, and its predictive aim is ÔÇťwhere faults will be,ÔÇŁ not causal mechanism. ţłÇciteţłéturn22view0ţłü

### When size ÔÇťstops matteringÔÇŁ after you control for process history

A similarly influential industrial analysis predicts future faults from **software change history** in a large, long-lived system. The dataset includes a **1.5M LOC subsystem**, **80 modules**, about **130,000** recorded changes, and predicts faults in a future **two-year interval** using only information available before that interval. ţłÇciteţłéturn21view0ţłü

Key size-related findings:

- Process measures (e.g., how often modules changed) outperform product snapshot measures (like LOC) in predicting fault incidence; the paper explicitly notes that **LOC is not helpful once number-of-changes information is included**, and that many complexity metrics add little because they correlate strongly with LOC in this dataset. ţłÇciteţłéturn21view0ţłü  
- The ÔÇťbestÔÇŁ model weights **large, recent changes** more heavily, implying that *change size* interacts with time (recency) and is central to fault potential. ţłÇciteţłéturn21view0ţłü  

This is one of the clearest cases where ÔÇťmodule/file sizeÔÇŁ alone is **not** the main actionable predictor once you have rich process data. ţłÇciteţłéturn21view0ţłü

### Nonlinear and ÔÇťcounter-intuitiveÔÇŁ sizeÔÇôdefect relationships

A major thread in the literature challenges simplistic linear thinking (ÔÇťbigger Ôçĺ worse densityÔÇŁ). A multi-project TSE study explicitly investigates the **functional form** of the sizeÔÇôdefect relationship using class-level data from **four large OO products** (including **Mozilla, Cn3d, JBoss, Eclipse**) and argues that the relationship is **logarithmic**: defect proneness increases with size but at a slower rate, making **smaller classes proportionally more problematic**. ţłÇciteţłéturn16view0ţłü

Two methodological contributions from this line of work are especially relevant:

- It critiques inference based on **defect density vs size** plots as potentially misleading (ratio/ÔÇťreciprocalÔÇŁ artifacts) and emphasizes modeling approaches that work with evolving entities and recurrent events rather than one snapshot. ţłÇciteţłéturn16view0ţłü  
- It provides a concrete cost-effectiveness illustration (e.g., allocating inspection resources to smaller classes can outperform focusing only on large classes in some projects), which is a stronger ÔÇťdecision framingÔÇŁ than a raw correlation. ţłÇciteţłéturn16view0ţłü  

Complementing that, a major industrial case study on faults and failures in two releases dedicates a full hypothesis set to size metrics (LOC) and discusses prior counter-intuitive findings: fault density can appear to **decrease with module size**, plausibly due to interface-fault distribution and the prevalence of small modules, while also warning that making modules ÔÇťtoo smallÔÇŁ can push complexity into interfaces. ţłÇciteţłéturn47view1ţłéturn46view0ţłü

### Confounding and collinearity: size as the ÔÇťhidden driverÔÇŁ

A seminal confounding demonstration analyzes a **C++ telecommunications framework** with **174 classes**, **192 field-failure faults**, and **14 programmers** as the development population, evaluating CK and related OO metrics against **fault-proneness**, with **LOC as the size covariate**. ţłÇciteţłéturn26view1ţłéturn26view3ţłéturn25view0ţłü

Two results are central:

- Many OO metrics are strongly correlated with size (example Spearman ¤ü values: WMC 0.88, RFC 0.88; others moderate), meaning that univariate validation can be ÔÇťoptimisticÔÇŁ by rediscovering size. ţłÇciteţłéturn26view3ţłü  
- After controlling for class size, the study reports that the previously ÔÇťvalidatedÔÇŁ associations disappear (in this dataset), implying that some metricÔćĺdefect claims are actually sizeÔćĺdefect in disguise. ţłÇciteţłéturn25view0ţłéturn26view1ţłü  

This doesnÔÇÖt show ÔÇťsize causes defects,ÔÇŁ but it strongly supports a practical recommendation: **any empirical study (or internal dashboard) claiming a metric predicts defects must show what happens when size is controlled.** ţłÇciteţłéturn25view0ţłéturn26view3ţłü

## Maintainability and change outcomes

### Method size and longitudinal maintenance effort proxies at scale

A recent MSR study directly targets ÔÇťwhat method size is maintainableÔÇŁ in **Java**, using **49 open-source projects** and extracting **785,606 methods**, excluding getters/setters and controlling for method age by excluding revisions/bugs after the first two years of a methodÔÇÖs life. ţłÇciteţłéturn40view0ţłéturn41view2ţłéturn42view3ţłü

Study design highlights:

- **Maintenance outcomes / proxies**: multiple method-level indicators such as number of revisions, added lines, diff size, edit distance, and bug-related commits (used as bug-proneness proxy). ţłÇciteţłéturn42view3ţłéturn40view0ţłü  
- **Statistics**: nonparametric KendallÔÇÖs ¤ä for correlation, Wilcoxon rank-sum for distribution differences, and CliffÔÇÖs delta as effect size (with explicit thresholds for negligible/small/medium/large). ţłÇciteţłéturn42view1ţłéturn42view2ţłéturn42view3ţłü  

Core results relevant to ÔÇťsizeÔÇŁ:

- Method SLOC correlates with both change- and bug-proneness indicators across projects (distributional evidence shown via CDFs of Kendall ¤ä). ţłÇciteţłéturn42view3ţłéturn40view0ţłü  
- A data-driven thresholding approach yields a practical recommendation: **keep methods ÔëĄ 24 SLOC**; differences between ÔÇťsmallÔÇŁ and ÔÇťmediumÔÇŁ methods are frequently statistically significant and often medium-to-large effect sizes, while differences at higher size bands tend to compress to negligible/small. ţłÇciteţłéturn42view2ţłéturn42view3ţłü  
- The study also constructs an inference about decomposition: groups of small methods (merge candidates) tend to be collectively less change/bug-prone than an equivalent-size single large method, supporting refactoring toward smaller methodsÔÇöwhile explicitly acknowledging coupling trade-offs. ţłÇciteţłéturn41view0ţłéturn42view3ţłéturn40view0ţłü  

This paper is unusually actionable because it combines scale, explicit thresholds, and effect-size reporting; its biggest validity risk is that ÔÇťmaintenance effortÔÇŁ is proxied (change/bug proneness) rather than directly measured as human-hours. ţłÇciteţłéturn40view0ţłéturn42view3ţłü

### Change size and defect density (industrial, large-scale binaries)

A rigorous industrial study of **relative code churn** shows how ÔÇťsize of changeÔÇŁ relates to defects, using Windows binary-level granularity with defect density (defects/KLOC). Dataset size is **2,465 binaries**, trained/test split methods are used, and multiple statistical approaches are compared. ţłÇciteţłéturn32view1ţłéturn32view1ţłéturn32view1ţłü

Key results:

- **Relative churn measures** show strong positive correlations with defects/KLOC (e.g., a churn ratio measure M1 has correlation **0.883** with defects/KLOC; other ratios are smaller but still positive). ţłÇciteţłéturn32view0ţłü  
- Regression using relative measures achieves high fit (e.g., **R┬▓ Ôëł 0.821** in one reported regression fit table), while **absolute churn measures** perform poorly in their PCA regression comparison (reported R┬▓ Ôëł 0.026). ţłÇciteţłéturn31view2ţłéturn32view1ţłü  

Interpretation for practitioners: ÔÇťhow big the change is relative to the componentÔÇŁ can matter more than raw churn totals, and many churn metrics are strongly intercorrelatedÔÇöso feature selection and careful interpretation are necessary. ţłÇciteţłéturn32view0ţłéturn32view1ţłü

### Change-induced defects across OSS and commercial projects

A large, multi-project ÔÇťjust-in-time quality assuranceÔÇŁ study examines **defect-inducing changes** using **11 projects**: six well-known OSS projects (Bugzilla, Columba, Mozilla, Eclipse JDT, Eclipse Platform, PostgreSQL) plus five commercial projects (C-1ÔÇŽC-5), mined from CVS history, in **C/C++ and/or Java**. ţłÇciteţłéturn27view1ţłéturn2view0ţłéturn30view0ţłü

Size-related independent variables include:

- Lines added (LA), lines deleted (LD), and file size before change (LT). ţłÇciteţłéturn30view0ţłéturn27view2ţłü  
- Diffusion/ÔÇťscopeÔÇŁ size such as number of files touched (NF), plus entropy-based spread metrics. ţłÇciteţłéturn30view0ţłéturn30view0ţłü  

Statistical approach:

- Logistic regression with odds ratios (including stepwise selection), plus an ÔÇťeffort-awareÔÇŁ modeling variant that accounts for inspection/review effort. ţłÇciteţłéturn29view0ţłéturn28view0ţłéturn30view1ţłü  

Main findings about ÔÇťsizeÔÇŁ are nuanced:

- Odds-ratio patterns differ by OSS vs commercial context; nevertheless, factors like **number of files (NF)** and **relative churn metrics** are repeatedly highlighted as influential for defect-inducing changes, with age effects differing across contexts. ţłÇciteţłéturn29view0ţłéturn30view1ţłü  
- The paper explicitly warns that effect direction and meaning depend on what other covariates are in the model and on defect-definition differences between OSS vs commercial reporting. ţłÇciteţłéturn29view0ţłéturn27view1ţłü  

## Comprehension cost and human factors evidence

Direct causal evidence linking ÔÇťfile sizeÔÇŁ to comprehension cost is rarer than defect modeling, because it requires controlled tasks and fine-grained measurement. One of the more informative controlled designs reanalyzes a prior dataset from professional maintenance tasks and decomposes effort into **activity-level costs**: reading, editing, searching, navigating. ţłÇciteţłéturn44view0ţłü

### Activity-level effort: file size vs change size vs smells

In a controlled maintenance experiment:

- **Participants and systems**: six professional developers; three maintenance tasks; four functionally equivalent Java systems; activity logs collected via an IDE plugin; activities inferred via annotation scheme. ţłÇciteţłéturn44view0ţłü  
- **Modeling**: multiple linear regression used to assess how smells, file size, and change size affect effort by activity type. ţłÇciteţłéturn44view0ţłü  
- **Main size-related result**: the **size of the changes performed** impacts the effort of *all* activities more than code smells and file size; additionally, **file size impacts reading and searching effort more than smells**, while smells can dominate file size for editing/navigating effort in that dataset. ţłÇciteţłéturn44view0ţłü  

This provides a practical ÔÇťcomprehension costÔÇŁ framing: **big changes are expensive across the board; large files primarily tax reading/searching**, even when other structural issues are present. ţłÇciteţłéturn44view0ţłü

## Causality, confounders, and replication

### What counts as ÔÇťcausalÔÇŁ evidence here

Most high-impact studies in this area are **observational** (mining historic repositories; industrial defect logs). They can estimate associations with controls but cannot fully establish causality because developers adapt behavior based on risk (e.g., more testing or scrutiny for large components), and because many determinants co-evolve (size, churn, coupling, ownership). ţłÇciteţłéturn21view0ţłéturn22view0ţłéturn2view0ţłéturn25view0ţłü

Controlled experiments exist (maintenance tasks with professionals), but they are typically small and context-specific, trading external for internal validity. ţłÇciteţłéturn44view0ţłü

### Recurrent confounders and why ÔÇťsmall is bestÔÇŁ can flip sign

The strongest empirical papers repeatedly surface these confounder classes:

- **Change history / churn**: frequency and size of edits can dominate fault prediction beyond static size. ţłÇciteţłéturn21view0ţłéturn47view1ţłü  
- **Prior faults and age**: prior defects and entity age influence future defects (sometimes older code has fewer faults once other factors are controlled). ţłÇciteţłéturn21view0ţłéturn22view0ţłéturn30view0ţłü  
- **Collinearity with other metrics**: OO metrics, complexity and token measures often correlate strongly with LOC, producing spurious ÔÇťvalidationÔÇŁ unless size is controlled. ţłÇciteţłéturn26view3ţłéturn25view0ţłéturn40view0ţłü  
- **Outcome definition**: fault *count* vs fault *density* vs defect-inducing *changes* vs CI build failures can yield different directional conclusions. ţłÇciteţłéturn22view0ţłéturn32view0ţłéturn38view0ţłéturn46view0ţłü  

This is why the literature contains apparently conflicting claims such as ÔÇťbigger modules have more faultsÔÇŁ and ÔÇťsmaller modules are proportionally more problematic.ÔÇŁ Both can be true simultaneously depending on whether one looks at totals or rates and how work is distributed. ţłÇciteţłéturn22view0ţłéturn16view0ţłéturn47view1ţłü

### Replication status and data accessibility

Replication is uneven:

- Several influential industrial system studies rely on proprietary data (e.g., multi-release industrial fault prediction; Windows binaries churn study; some commercial projects in JIT defect prediction), limiting independent replication. ţłÇciteţłéturn22view0ţłéturn32view1ţłéturn27view1ţłü  
- Some newer MSR work provides explicit replication hooks via public datasets or code packages: the CI build-failures-at-scale study uses a named TravisTorrent snapshot and documents dataset composition; the maintainable-method-size study points to a public dataset repository. ţłÇciteţłéturn39view3ţłéturn40view0ţłéturn41view2ţłü

### Study summary table

| CI build failures at scale (MSR) ţłÇciteţłéturn38view0ţłéturn39view3ţłü | 2017 | TravisTorrent snapshot; **1,090** Java/Ruby projects; **3.6M builds** analyzed ţłÇciteţłéturn39view3ţłéturn39view1ţłü | Task/build size proxies: source code churn (SCC), changed files (FLC), built commits (BCB) ţłÇciteţłéturn38view0ţłü | Build result: successful vs unsuccessful ţłÇciteţłéturn38view0ţłéturn39view3ţłü | MannÔÇôWhitneyÔÇôWilcoxon; chi-squared; CohenÔÇÖs d; large-scale comparative analysis ţłÇciteţłéturn38view0ţłü | SCC dÔëł**0.34** (medium); FLC dÔëł**0.36** (medium); TCC dÔëł**0.213** (small); all statistically significant for SCC/FLC differences ţłÇciteţłéturn38view0ţłü | Build failure Ôëá production failure; build data quality and filtering choices; task definition (pushÔćĺtask) may be imperfect ţłÇciteţłéturn39view1ţłéturn38view0ţłü |
| Maintainable method size in Java (MSR) ţłÇciteţłéturn40view0ţłéturn41view2ţłéturn42view3ţłü | 2022 | **49 OSS Java projects**; **785,606 methods**; controls for age, removes getters/setters ţłÇciteţłéturn41view2ţłéturn42view3ţłü | Method SLOC; size categories derived from benchmark-threshold method ţłÇciteţłéturn42view3ţłéturn41view0ţłü | Change & bug-proneness proxies (#revisions, diff/edit metrics, buggy commits); also examines other quality metrics under size control ţłÇciteţłéturn42view3ţłéturn40view0ţłü | Kendall ¤ä; Wilcoxon; CliffÔÇÖs ╬┤; cross-project distributional reporting ţłÇciteţłéturn42view3ţłéturn42view1ţłéturn42view2ţłü | Recommends **ÔëĄ24 SLOC**; smallÔćömedium differences often medium/large effect sizes; larger band differences compress; decomposition analysis suggests refactoring large methods helps overall maintenance indicators ţłÇciteţłéturn42view3ţłéturn41view0ţłü | Proxy outcomes; bug labeling via commit heuristics has error; decomposition inference is indirect; OSS-only external validity caveat ţłÇciteţłéturn40view0ţłéturn42view3ţłü |
| Code smells and maintenance activities at activity level (SANER) ţłÇciteţłéturn44view0ţłü | 2016 | Controlled setting: 4 functionally equivalent Java systems; 6 professionals; activity logs via IDE plugin ţłÇciteţłéturn44view0ţłü | File size; **change size** (size of changes made); compares with smell presence ţłÇciteţłéturn44view0ţłü | Activity effort (reading, editing, searching, navigating) as comprehension/maintenance cost ţłÇciteţłéturn44view0ţłü | Multiple linear regression; compares relative contribution of predictors ţłÇciteţłéturn44view0ţłü | Change size impacts all activities more than file size; file size impacts reading/searching more than smells; some smells surpass file size for edit/navigate ţłÇciteţłéturn44view0ţłü | Small-N; task/system specificity; effort measurement depends on logging/annotation; not generalizable alone but strong mechanistic insight ţłÇciteţłéturn44view0ţłü |

### Charts

#### Timeline of key studies

```mermaid
timeline
  title Key empirical studies connecting size to quality outcomes
  2000 : Fault incidence predicted from change history (process dominates LOC)
  2000 : Faults/failures analysis; size vs fault density pitfalls; prerelease Ôëá postrelease
  2001 : OO metric validity challenged by size confounding
  2005 : Fault location & counts in industrial releases; LOC near-proportional
  2005 : Relative churn correlates strongly with defect density (industrial binaries)
  2009 : SizeÔÇôdefect functional form is sublinear across multiple OO products
  2013 : Change-level defect-inducing risk linked to change size and diffusion
  2016 : Maintenance activity effort shows file size affects reading/searching; change size dominates
  2017 : CI build failures at scale relate to changed lines/files with smallÔÇômedium effects
  2022 : Method-level maintainability thresholds; ÔëĄ24 SLOC guideline with effect sizes
```

(See the cited primary papers for each point.) ţłÇciteţłéturn21view0ţłéturn46view0ţłéturn25view0ţłéturn22view0ţłéturn32view0ţłéturn16view0ţłéturn2view0ţłéturn44view0ţłéturn38view0ţłéturn40view0ţłü

These are not directly comparable across study designs (correlation vs standardized mean difference), but they give a concrete feel for magnitude in two common reporting families.

**A. Spearman ¤ü for (relative churn metric Ôćĺ defects/KLOC)** (industrial binaries study)

### Mermaid model of relationships between variables

```mermaid
flowchart LR
  A[Static size of unit\nLOC/SLOC per method/file/class] -->|often +| Q1[Absolute defect count]
  A -->|ambiguous due to denominators| Q2[Defect density]
  A -->|+ reading/search effort| H1[Comprehension / activity cost]
  A -->|correlates with| M[Other metrics\ncomplexity, token counts,\ncoupling proxies]

  C[Change size\nlines added/deleted,\nfiles touched] -->|often +| Q3[Defect-inducing change risk]
  C -->|often +| Q4[CI/build failure risk]
  C -->|dominant +| H1

  P[Process/history\n#changes, recency,\nprior faults, age] -->|often +| Q1
  P -->|often +| Q3
  P -->|often +| Q4

  Z[Confounders / context\nlanguage, ownership,\ntesting intensity,\nrelease stage] --> Q1
  Z --> Q3
  Z --> Q4
  Z --> H1

  M -->|collinearity| A
  M -->|spurious validation if size not controlled| Q1
```

This structure is directly motivated by empirical findings where (i) LOC predicts fault counts in some settings, (ii) churn/change history dominates in others, and (iii) size confounds many metrics unless modeled explicitly. ţłÇciteţłéturn22view0ţłéturn21view0ţłéturn25view0ţłéturn2view0ţłéturn44view0ţłéturn38view0ţłü

### Practical framing and recommended wording

The most defensible, non-dogmatic guidance is conditional:

When ÔÇťsmallerÔÇŁ tends to help:

- When the unit is a **method** or similarly local unit, evidence supports that keeping it below a practical threshold can reduce change/bug-proneness proxies, with reported medium-to-large effect sizes at smallÔćĺmedium transitions (e.g., ÔëĄ24 SLOC in one large Java study). ţłÇciteţłéturn42view3ţłéturn42view2ţłéturn40view0ţłü  
- When the unit is a **change/PR/build task**, smaller scope (fewer lines/files/commits) is repeatedly associated with lower defect-inducing and build-failure risk in large MSR datasets. ţłÇciteţłéturn30view0ţłéturn30view1ţłéturn38view0ţłü  

When ÔÇťsmallerÔÇŁ does **not** reliably mean better:

- For **defect density**, several influential analyses argue the sizeÔÇôdensity relationship can be counter-intuitive or artifact-prone; conclusions depend heavily on denominators and on where complexity is placed (interfaces vs bodies). ţłÇciteţłéturn47view1ţłéturn16view0ţłéturn46view0ţłü  
- For **metric dashboards**, a major validity threat is that many ÔÇťquality metricsÔÇŁ are proxies for size; without controlling for size, you may mistakenly treat size as a separate causal factor (or vice versa). ţłÇciteţłéturn25view0ţłéturn26view3ţłéturn42view3ţłü  

Trade-offs to state explicitly:

- Splitting code can reduce local reasoning load, but may increase **navigation and coupling/interface load**; empirical work on activity effort suggests file size impacts reading/searching, while other structural factors can dominate editing/navigating and change size dominates across activities. ţłÇciteţłéturn44view0ţłéturn41view0ţłü  
- ÔÇťMake files tinyÔÇŁ may increase total number of artifacts and dependency edges; the best evidence supports **purposeful decomposition** (e.g., ÔÇťkeep methods small enough to reason about; avoid giant changesÔÇŁ), not universal minification. ţłÇciteţłéturn40view0ţłéturn44view0ţłéturn16view0ţłü  

Recommended wording (evidence-aligned):

- **Avoid:** ÔÇťLarge files are bad; always split.ÔÇŁ  
- **Prefer:** ÔÇťSize is a useful *risk signal*. Keep units small enough to review/understand, but evaluate in context (churn, coupling, history, ownership). Use size thresholds as guardrails, not absolutes.ÔÇŁ ţłÇciteţłéturn21view0ţłéturn25view0ţłéturn40view0ţłéturn44view0ţłéturn38view0ţłü
